msg:Due to the epidemic, I dare not go out of town now, so I want to find a hotel in Shanghai to relax for two days. I thought that Shanghai should be one level higher than other hotels of the same level in other places in terms of management and service, but it turned out that there are too many flaws, so I will complain about the ones I can think of first.

First, there are too many people checking in, and there is no one outside the counter to maintain order. A bunch of old people gathered around the front desk, and the young staff at the counter looked overwhelmed. The person behind me jumped in line to check in at the counter, and no one took care of it at all. After I checked in, the waiter didn't tell me which elevator to take, so I asked an employee who was chatting with foreign employees. She pointed me to the restaurant without asking my room number, and only when I went up did I realize I was going the wrong way. , my room has to go back to the third floor and cross the corridor to the other side of the building. Only later did I know that the customer service is divided into T1 and T2, but there is no sign in the lobby, and no staff has taken this into account. The employees I met in the elevator bowed their heads and played with their mobile phones the whole time without saying hello. There is no basic courtesy.

Second, I felt very hot when I entered the room. I found that the air conditioner could not adjust the temperature, and I could not adjust the temperature. Moreover, the room only had floor-to-ceiling windows on three sides, no small windows, and no ventilation. The room temperature was kept at 28-29 degrees. It is both wasteful and not considered for the guests.

Third, the toilet design is speechless. When the toilet lid is opened, the flush button is covered, which means that the toilet cannot be flushed until the toilet lid is put down. Why is there such an anti-human design!

Fourth, there is a thin layer of ash in the entire room where there is a desktop, the first day and the second day, and the hygiene standard is low.

Fifth, there are not many varieties of breakfast, and the waiter's attitude is not good. I asked if there were wontons. A female employee said no without raising her head. I said help me with a bowl of noodles. What I'm looking for is that I don't cook noodles, and I'm reluctant to cook noodles after being taught a few words by the person in charge.

As a hotel next to the National Exhibition and Convention Center, there must be a lot of exhibitors who usually stay there. Maybe there are foreign friends staying at the CIIE. How can it reflect Shanghai's standards, or will it be treated differently?
